  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5c1ea38d-ac0c-4b1b-8de1-4dd2c68b376e'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer1419404506508129286">You don't have to be a teenager to appreciate the humorous and often self-absorbed ravings found in 14-year-old Georgia Nicolson's diary, but it certainly helps. Now fans of <i>Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging</i> -- Georgia's first set of hilarious musings on life -- can get another peek into the mind of this wryly inquisitive English lass in the appealing sequel: <i>On the </i></span>
  <span id="freeText1419404506508129286" style="display:none">You don't have to be a teenager to appreciate the humorous and often self-absorbed ravings found in 14-year-old Georgia Nicolson's diary, but it certainly helps. Now fans of <i>Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging</i> -- Georgia's first set of hilarious musings on life -- can get another peek into the mind of this wryly inquisitive English lass in the appealing sequel: <i>On the Bright Side, I'm Now the Girlfriend of a Sex God.</i><br /><p><br />As the title implies, Georgia has snagged herself a sex god in the form of Robbie, the boy of her dreams. Now that they've indulged in a bit of "full-frontal snogging," Georgia turns her attention to advancing the relationship. But things quickly go wrong when she learns that her father's new job may necessitate a move to New Zealand. Crestfallen, Georgia feels her life might as well be over. Then, miraculously, the dreaded move is cancelled, and things seem to be getting better -- at least until 17-year-old Robbie decides to break up with Georgia because he's bothered by the difference in their ages. <br /></p><p><br />Borrowing freely from her mum's closet and advice books, even as she's steadfastly discounting everything her mum says, a crushed but determined Georgia comes up with a scheme to win Robbie back. As usual, nothing goes as planned, and life is further complicated by Georgia's temperamental cat, Angus (who's having a few amorous leanings of his own), and her baby sister, Libby, whose fascination with (and lack of control over) her bodily functions leads to several intriguing mishaps. Of course, there are other disasters, too: a quick-tan lotion that turns Georgia's legs orange, a run-in with the aptly named Bummer sisters, and friends who insist on focusing on their own problems from time to time.<br /></p><p><br />Who knew the angst of adolescence could be so much fun? This Georgia's-eye view of teenage life is wonderfully egocentric and side-splittingly funny. And despite the occasional language barrier (a glossary of terms is provided in the back of the book), Georgia's thoughts and experiences will prove universally recognizable to anyone who is, or has ever been, a teenager. <br /></p><p>
  <br />
  <i>--Beth Amos</i>
</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="1419404506508129286" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Relaxing, entertaining and makes me thrilled to not only have me out of my teen years, but my kids, too. 😊</span>

    <a title="Nicola " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2461560-nicola"><img alt="Nicola " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385858279p2/2461560.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/202704997?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicola " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicola " href="/user/show/2461560-nicola">Nicola </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007218684" href="/book/show/864762.It_s_OK_I_m_Wearing_Really_Big_Knickers">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2461560-nicola?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2461560-nicola?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2461560-nicola?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer202704997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11460206443637635020">This book was every bit as fun as I expected it to be. This series is just really cute, funny and light-hearted. Georgia is simply hilarious and I never tire of her dramatic reactions. Her witty diary entries are infectious and I find them impossible to look away from. This installment did drag at parts but it was mostly as entertaining and amusing as the first. I'm certainly looking forward to see what else is in store for Georgia. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1340730671278770540"><i> Still, I refuse to be upset. I will remain calm beneath my egg and olive oil face mask. </i> <br/><br/>Hilarious. <b> Georgia Nicolson is an icon. </b> Although not a lot happens in this book (and I preferred the first one), it’s really funny and witty. Don’t take this book too seriously. I’ve seen a lot of people complaining that Georgia is only focused on her nose and on her boyfriend. And…. Yeah, she is. <u>That’s the point.</u> She’s an angsty teenager, kinda mean to her friends, and in love with a Sex God. I was laug</span>
  <span id="freeText1340730671278770540" style="display:none"><i> Still, I refuse to be upset. I will remain calm beneath my egg and olive oil face mask. </i> <br /><br />Hilarious. <b> Georgia Nicolson is an icon. </b> Although not a lot happens in this book (and I preferred the first one), it’s really funny and witty. Don’t take this book too seriously. I’ve seen a lot of people complaining that Georgia is only focused on her nose and on her boyfriend. And…. Yeah, she is. <u>That’s the point.</u> She’s an angsty teenager, kinda mean to her friends, and in love with a Sex God. I was laughing reading this book and I mean <i> actually laughing </i>. Georgia is a well of golden sassy quotes. <br /><br /><i> I can’t believe Jas. She is dead to me. Like in the Bible, when somebody goes off and becomes a prostitute or something. She is now the girl who has no name. </i><br /><br /><i> “It’s me, Jas.” “Oh...What do YOU want?” “I’ve just called to see how you are.” I said, “Dead actually, I died a few hours ago. Goodbye.” </i><br /><br />Also thanks to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/34484816" rel="nofollow noopener">Holly</a> for recommending this book series ☀️</span>

  <span id="freeText17456978244328753538" style="display:none"><strong>4 LAUGH AT LOUD STARS!</strong><br /><br /><em>“He said, 'Hi, gorgeous,' which I think is nice. I admire honesty.”</em><br /> <br />So, once again Georgia Nicolson made laugh a lot with her occurences. She got all red-faced, which in Jas's case is very red indeed. It made me feel much better. Violence may be the answer to the world's problems. I may write to the Dalai Lama and suggest he tries my new approach.”</em><br /><br />She is a BULLY! Everything is against Jas, and poor her that I don't know how they still friends. I don't remember my sister or me doing those things. Plus her mother is always ignoring her like she doesn't care, i hate it.<br /><br /><em>“Boys are like elastic bands... Boys are different from girls. Girls like to be cozy all the time but boys don't. First of all, they like to get all close to you like a coiled-up rubber band, but after a while, they get fed up with being too coiled and need to stretch away to their full stretchiness. Then, after a bit of on-their-own strategy, they ping back to be close to you.”</em><br /><br />I'm trying to understand Georgia's way, I do, but I can't. Is she is so in love with Robbie, why is she so stupid in front of him. I guess that she turns more than jelly thanks to love? <em>Sacré Bleu!</em> Why I'm still reading this? I don't know. Will I keep reading it? <em>Sí</em>.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer133137249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18209241509634899097">What I like most about the Georgia Nicolson series is that it doesn’t try to be posh. It strives for absurdosity and succeeds. This installment picked up where <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/402013.Angus__Thongs_and_Full_Frontal_Snogging__Confessions_of_Georgia_Nicolson___1_' title='Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging (Confessions of Georgia Nicolson, #1) by Louise Rennison' rel='nofollow noopener'>Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging</a> left off, with Georgia losing the SG and protesting a move to Kiwi-a-gogo Land (a.k.a. New Zealand). From there, it only gets crazier: cat mating, Elastic Band theory, Dr. George Clooney, the German language, a wheelbarrow, etc. <br/><br/>Georgia is like the friend you want to dope slap, but just shake your h</span>
  <span id="freeText18209241509634899097" style="display:none">What I like most about the Georgia Nicolson series is that it doesn’t try to be posh. It strives for absurdosity and succeeds. This installment picked up where <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/402013.Angus__Thongs_and_Full_Frontal_Snogging__Confessions_of_Georgia_Nicolson___1_" title="Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging (Confessions of Georgia Nicolson, #1) by Louise Rennison" rel="nofollow noopener">Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging</a> left off, with Georgia losing the SG and protesting a move to Kiwi-a-gogo Land (a.k.a. New Zealand). From there, it only gets crazier: cat mating, Elastic Band theory, Dr. George Clooney, the German language, a wheelbarrow, etc. <br /><br />Georgia is like the friend you want to dope slap, but just shake your head and laugh at instead because you realize whatever you do won’t make a lick of difference. She’s going to do mad things no matter what. That’s why glimpses of her nicer side are so surprising. Deep down beneath the stupidity and shallowness and mascara is a good person. Deep, deep down. <br /><br />Anyway, is it wrong that I dislike the SG and think Georgia should beg Dave the Laugh (a.k.a. best boyfriend EVER) to take her back? <i>Nein</i>? Thought so.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1710557-amy?shelf=give-me-my-time-back">give-me-my-time-back</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41608788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7142833494762483021">This was given to me by a friend. I actually read the first book by this author, which I thought was Bridget Jones but with teenage angst. The best character was Angus the wild cat. The humor was there but wore thin pretty quickly. The best thing about this was the title, IMO.<br/><br/>Amazon Editorial Review:<br/><br/>Fourteen-year-old Georgia Nicolson is back in British author Louise Rennison's irreverent, laugh-out-loud sequel to the Michael L. Printz Honor Book Angus, Thongs, and Full-Frontal Snogging. Written </span>
  <span id="freeText7142833494762483021" style="display:none">This was given to me by a friend. I actually read the first book by this author, which I thought was Bridget Jones but with teenage angst. The best character was Angus the wild cat. The humor was there but wore thin pretty quickly. The best thing about this was the title, IMO.<br /><br />Amazon Editorial Review:<br /><br />Fourteen-year-old Georgia Nicolson is back in British author Louise Rennison's irreverent, laugh-out-loud sequel to the Michael L. Printz Honor Book Angus, Thongs, and Full-Frontal Snogging. Written in diary form, these truly hilarious books chronicle the often minute-by-minute, very dramatic, and significant flip-flops of a teenager's psyche.<br /><br />7:18 p.m.<br />My eyes are all swollen up like mice eyes from crying. Even my nose is swollen. It's not small at the best of times, but now it looks like I've got three cheeks. Marvelous. Thank you, God.<br /><br />9:00 p.m.<br />I'll never get over this.<br /><br />9:10 p.m.<br />Time goes very slowly when you're suicidal.<br /><br />What tragedy has her so distraught? Her parents have told her she's moving to New Zealand just when she's managed to snog (kiss--look it up in the glossary) the SG (Sex God, a.k.a Robbie). This is of course not the only source of drama in Georgia's eventful life. Her half Scottish wildcat, Angus, who is the size of a small Labrador, herds the poodles next door and terrorizes the neighborhood. Her little sister, Libby, who is slightly mad, stores her "pooey knickers" and her scuba-diving Barbie doll in Georgia's bed. Her mother (from whom she inherited her orangutan eyebrow gene and possibly her "gigantic basoomas") is clearly inhabiting Earth solely to make her life miserable, and even her best friend Jas is "half girl, half turnip."<br /><br />Despite the fact that she's spared from going to "Kiwi-a-gogo land," things don't get much better for Georgia. She's suspended for a childish prank right before her dad returns from New Zealand, she falls in love with the SG who dumps her for being too young, and Dave, the "red-herring" boyfriend she's using to make the SG jealous calls her a "heartless whatsit." And, she continues, "the spot on my bum is probably a boil. I wonder what Buddha would do now?" Rennison's comedic timing is brilliant. Adolescent angst ("I hope I am not driven to the brink of madness by grief") vanishes less than an hour later ("Angus can fetch sticks!!!") and sometimes even sooner. (Warning: Do not read this book while riding a train or bus unless you don't care what people think of intermittent explosive laughter. Seriously.) (Ages 12 and older) --Karin Snelson</span>
  <a data-text-id="7142833494762483021" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/265714370?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Silvia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Silvia" href="/user/show/6227263-silvia">Silvia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780641925771" href="/book/show/7740127-on-the-bright-side-i-m-now-the-girlfriend-of-a-sex-god">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer265714370" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9140133586874384852">I was in the library looking for a book to read, and I came across this one that I had actually failed at finding before. Georgia Nicolson comes back as funny as ever, she is now the girlfriend of Robbie (who she calls Sex God) and she thinks of nothing but snogging him. When he dumps her for being "too young" she tries to finds a way to get him back. There were many quotes that I love in the book, but one of my favourites was "What is there to laugh at? I am on the rack of love. Life is a sham </span>
  <span id="freeText9140133586874384852" style="display:none">I was in the library looking for a book to read, and I came across this one that I had actually failed at finding before. Georgia Nicolson comes back as funny as ever, she is now the girlfriend of Robbie (who she calls Sex God) and she thinks of nothing but snogging him. When he dumps her for being "too young" she tries to finds a way to get him back. There were many quotes that I love in the book, but one of my favourites was "What is there to laugh at? I am on the rack of love. Life is a sham and a facsimile and a farce." The quote shows Georgia's frustration with her life at the moment, but also shows a bit of her comical side. I loved how the author wrote in first-person, she did a great job writing down the thoughts of a 14 year old. It was fun reading the bits she wrote in French and in German also. I recommend this book to girls in need of a laugh, and who are experiencing boy problems. This book doesn't offer a good solution to those problems, but it sure lets you laugh non-stop about them. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9140133586874384852" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3820795609799489348"><b> 3.5 stars </b> <br/><br/>Georgia is quite literally the description of a self-centred, over-dramatic teenager, who only wants all the attention on her and no one else, which is pretty annoying but simply accurate on how most of the young teenagers are. The boo</span>
  <span id="freeText3820795609799489348" style="display:none"><b> 3.5 stars </b> <br /><br />Georgia is quite literally the description of a self-centred, over-dramatic teenager, who only wants all the attention on her and no one else, which is pretty annoying but simply accurate on how most of the young teenagers are. Even though this was the case and that I sometimes I cringed at the use of words (this book is written as a diary of a 14 years old girl so vocabulary included), I couldn't stop reading. <br /><br />I found myself turning pages and turning pages and turning pages. The books are enormously different from the movie, which I LOVED, but they're still enjoyable nonetheless. Even if Georgia's behaviour it's kinda annoying sometimes. <br />Also Libby, Georgia's baby sister, I find incredibly annoying. She is so disgusting and irritating hahaha I don't even know how to put it in words. Either way, I do enjoy reading this series and as they are super quick reads, I'm sure I'll be finishing this series off before I know it!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780060288723" href="/book/show/1036555.On_the_Bright_Side_I_m_Now_the_Girlfriend_of_a_Sex_God">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1147994413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2678165430376064058"><b>Actual rating:</b> 1.5 stars<br/><br/><b>Initial thoughts:</b> My intention was to read all the books in the series. I don't think that's gonna happen after all. The first book was half-way entertaining. This second one was tiresome to read. There were some amusing moments but on the whole it wasn't all that funny. Georgia is beyond self-absorbed. Sure, it's her diary and she's 14 but she shows no respect for anyone in her life, not even her best friend. In fact, she displays no true affection for her best friend at</span>
  <span id="freeText2678165430376064058" style="display:none"><b>Actual rating:</b> 1.5 stars<br /><br /><b>Initial thoughts:</b> My intention was to read all the books in the series. I don't think that's gonna happen after all. The first book was half-way entertaining. This second one was tiresome to read. There were some amusing moments but on the whole it wasn't all that funny. Georgia is beyond self-absorbed. Sure, it's her diary and she's 14 but she shows no respect for anyone in her life, not even her best friend. In fact, she displays no true affection for her best friend at all. She's incredibly rude to people around her in the name of humour. I'm not buying it. The prose annoyed me too with all these made up words and repetitions. The only strength I found was the consistency of Georgia's character, which I didn't even like reading anymore.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IIVUnntH5RCLRq4c1Oj7OSi3MJGyePLmBs1wk82n0fLLEbdVqbWA1bjGLBupCwsQ+siO//6BZTVhL6MmiF/7Vw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TGAJMv9tAXHWn9DQJYlGeGR2VNuA9EQd6EygxxM6b2qn9Or5LZ9ktOUfUtdYarZRtgnqtcwN086PrnNyVsJFzw==')})
  }
